<p><b>Braunschweig</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈbʁaʊ̯nʃvaɪ̯k]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Braunschweig.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/De-Braunschweig.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Braunschweig.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Low_German" title="Low German">Low German</a>: <i>Brunswiek</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ˈbrɔˑnsviːk]</a></span>), also called <b>Brunswick</b> in English,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> is a city of 252,768 people (as of 31 December 2015),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> located in the state of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a>, Germany. It is situated north of the <a href="/wiki/Harz" title="Harz">Harz</a> mountains at the furthest navigable point of the <a href="/wiki/Oker" title="Oker">Oker</a> river, which connects to the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> via the rivers <a href="/wiki/Aller" title="Aller">Aller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weser" title="Weser">Weser</a>.</p>
<p>A powerful and influential centre of commerce in medieval Germany, Braunschweig was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> from the 13th until the 17th century. It was the capital city of three successive states: the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Principality of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Principality of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel</a> (1269–1432, 1754–1807 and 1813–1814), the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brunswick" title="Duchy of Brunswick">Duchy of Brunswick</a> (1814–1918) and the <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Brunswick" title="Free State of Brunswick">Free State of Brunswick</a> (1918–1946).</p>
<p>Today, Braunschweig is the second largest city in Lower Saxony and a major centre of <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific research</a> and development.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Braunschweig" title="Timeline of Braunschweig">Timeline of Braunschweig</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg/220px-BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg/330px-BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg/440px-BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5109" data-file-height="3406" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BurgDankwarderode2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dankwarderode Castle</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_and_early_history">Foundation and early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation and early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The date and circumstances of the town's foundation are unknown. Tradition maintains that Braunschweig was created through the merger of two settlements, one founded by <a href="/wiki/Bruno,_Duke_of_Saxony" title="Bruno, Duke of Saxony">Brun(o)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Saxon_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Saxon people">Saxon</a> count who died in 880, on one side of the river Oker – the legend gives the year 861 for the foundation – and the other the settlement of a legendary Count Dankward, after whom <a href="/wiki/Dankwarderode_Castle" title="Dankwarderode Castle">Dankwarderode Castle</a> <i>(Dankward's clearing)</i>, which was reconstructed in the 19th century, is named.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-braunschweig.de_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-braunschweig.de-7">[7]</a></sup> The town's original name of <i>Brunswik</i> is a combination of the name Bruno and <a href="/wiki/Low_German_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Low German language">Low German</a> <i>wik</i>, a place where merchants rested and stored their goods. The town's name therefore indicates an ideal resting-place, as it lay by a ford across the Oker River. Another explanation of the city's name is that it comes from <i>Brand</i>, or burning, indicating a place which developed after the landscape was cleared through burning.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The city was first mentioned in documents from the St. Magni Church from 1031, which give the city's name as <i>Brunesguik</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-braunschweig.de_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-braunschweig.de-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_and_early_modern_period">Middle Ages and early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages and early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg/220px-Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg" width="220" height="56" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg/330px-Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg/440px-Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2039" data-file-height="515" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braun_Braunschweig_UBHD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brunswick_cathedral.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Brunswick_cathedral.JPG/220px-Brunswick_cathedral.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Brunswick_cathedral.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brunswick_cathedral.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brunswick Cathedral, St. Blasius, with lion statue</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Up to the 12th century, Braunschweig was ruled by the Saxon noble family of the <a href="/wiki/Brunonids" title="Brunonids">Brunonids</a>, then, through marriage, it fell to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Welf" title="House of Welf">House of Welf</a>. In 1142 <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Lion" title="Henry the Lion">Henry the Lion</a> of the House of Welf became duke of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Saxony" title="Duchy of Saxony">Saxony</a> and made Braunschweig the capital of his state (which, from 1156 on, also included the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Duchy of Bavaria</a>). He turned Dankwarderode Castle, the residence of the counts of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Brunswick" title="County of Brunswick">Brunswick</a>, into his own <i><a href="/wiki/Kaiserpfalz" title="Kaiserpfalz">Pfalz</a></i> and developed the city further to represent his authority. Under Henry's rule the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Cathedral" title="Brunswick Cathedral">Cathedral</a> of St. Blasius was built and he also had the statue of a lion, his heraldic animal, erected in front of the castle. The <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Lion" title="Brunswick Lion">lion</a> subsequently became the city's landmark.</p>
<p>Henry the Lion became so powerful that he dared to refuse military aid to the emperor <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_Barbarossa" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick I Barbarossa">Frederick I Barbarossa</a>, which led to his banishment in 1182. Henry went into exile in England. He had previously established ties to the English crown in 1168, through his marriage to King <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II of England</a>'s daughter <a href="/wiki/Matilda_of_England,_Duchess_of_Saxony" title="Matilda of England, Duchess of Saxony">Matilda</a>, sister of <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard the Lionheart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> However, his son <a href="/wiki/Otto_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto</a>, who could regain influence and was eventually crowned <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>, continued to foster the city's development.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> Braunschweig was an important center of trade, one of the economic and political centers in Northern Europe and a member of the Hanseatic League from the 13th century to the middle of the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> By the year 1600, Braunschweig was the seventh largest city in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Although formally one of the residences of the rulers of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Duchy of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Duchy of Brunswick-Lüneburg</a>, a constituent state of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, Braunschweig was <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> ruled independently by a powerful class of <a href="/wiki/Patrician_(post-Roman_Europe)" title="Patrician (post-Roman Europe)">patricians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">guilds</a> throughout much of the <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">Early modern period</a>. Because of the growing power of Braunschweig's <a href="/wiki/Medieval_bourgeoisie" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval bourgeoisie">burghers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Principality of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Princes of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel</a>, who ruled over one of the subdivisions of Brunswick-Lüneburg, finally moved their <i><a href="/wiki/Residenz" title="Residenz">Residenz</a></i> out of the city and to the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Wolfenbüttel">Wolfenbüttel</a> in 1432.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The Princes of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel didn't regain control over the city until the late 17th century, when <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_Augustus,_Duke_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Rudolph Augustus, Duke of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Rudolph Augustus, Duke of Brunswick-Lüneburg</a>, took the city by siege.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In the 18th century Braunschweig was not only a political, but also a cultural centre. Influenced by the philosophy of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a>, dukes like <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Ulrich,_Duke_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Anthony Ulrich, Duke of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Anthony Ulrich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_I,_Duke_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Charles I, Duke of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Charles I</a> became patrons of the arts and sciences. In 1745 Charles I founded the <i>Collegium Carolinum</i>, predecessor of the <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_University_of_Technology" title="Braunschweig University of Technology">Braunschweig University of Technology</a>, and in 1753 he moved the ducal residence back to Braunschweig. With this he attracted poets and thinkers such as <a href="/wiki/Gotthold_Ephraim_Lessing" title="Gotthold Ephraim Lessing">Lessing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Anton_Leisewitz" title="Johann Anton Leisewitz">Leisewitz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jakob_Mauvillon" title="Jakob Mauvillon">Jakob Mauvillon</a> to his court and the city.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Emilia_Galotti" title="Emilia Galotti">Emilia Galotti</a></i> by Lessing and <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Goethe</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Goethe%27s_Faust" title="Goethe's Faust">Faust</a></i> were performed for the first time in Braunschweig.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_(2005).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_%282005%29.JPG/220px-Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_%282005%29.JPG" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_%282005%29.JPG/330px-Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_%282005%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_%282005%29.JPG/440px-Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_%282005%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1563" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig_Brunswick_BS-Landtag_(2005).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Landschaftliches Haus</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Landtag" title="Landtag">Landtag</a></i> building of the Duchy and the Free State of Brunswick.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1806, the city was captured by the <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> and became part of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleonic</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Westphalia" title="Kingdom of Westphalia">Kingdom of Westphalia</a> in 1807. The exiled duke <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William,_Duke_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Frederick William, Duke of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Frederick William</a> raised a volunteer corps, the <a href="/wiki/Black_Brunswickers" title="Black Brunswickers">Black Brunswickers</a>, that fought the French in several battles.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarck1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarck1-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> in 1815, Braunschweig was made capital of the reestablished independent <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brunswick" title="Duchy of Brunswick">Duchy of Brunswick</a>, later a constituent state of the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> from 1871. In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/July_Revolution" title="July Revolution">July Revolution</a> in 1830, in Brunswick duke <a href="/wiki/Charles_II,_Duke_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles II, Duke of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Charles II</a> was forced to abdicate. His <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolutist</a> governing style had peviously alienated the nobility and <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a>, while the lower classes were disaffected by the bad economic situation. During the night of 7–8 September 1830, the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Palace" title="Brunswick Palace">ducal palace</a> in Braunschweig was stormed by an angry mob, set on fire and destroyed completely.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Charles was succeeded by his brother <a href="/wiki/William_VIII,_Duke_of_Brunswick" class="mw-redirect" title="William VIII, Duke of Brunswick">William VIII</a>. During William's reign, liberal reforms were made and Brunswick's parliament was strengthened.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialisation</a> caused a rapid growth of population in the city, eventually causing Braunschweig to be for the first time significantly enlarged beyond its medieval <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">fortifications</a> and the river Oker.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> On 1 December 1838, the first section of the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick%E2%80%93Bad_Harzburg_railway" title="Brunswick–Bad Harzburg railway">Brunswick–Bad Harzburg railway</a> line connecting Braunschweig and Wolfenbüttel opened as the first railway line in Northern Germany, operated by the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brunswick_State_Railway" title="Duchy of Brunswick State Railway">Duchy of Brunswick State Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_to_mid-20th_century">Early to mid-20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early to mid-20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Braunschweig.jpg/220px-Braunschweig.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Braunschweig.jpg/330px-Braunschweig.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Braunschweig.jpg/440px-Braunschweig.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3508" data-file-height="2497" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Braunschweig around 1900.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig15101944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Braunschweig15101944.jpg/220px-Braunschweig15101944.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Braunschweig15101944.jpg/330px-Braunschweig15101944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Braunschweig15101944.jpg/440px-Braunschweig15101944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="589" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig15101944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Braunschweig on the night of 15 October 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 8 November 1918, at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a> <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_council" title="Workers' council">Workers' council</a> forced Duke <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Augustus,_Duke_of_Brunswick" title="Ernest Augustus, Duke of Brunswick">Ernest Augustus</a> to abdicate.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> On 10 November, the council proclaimed the Socialist Republic of Brunswick under one-party government by the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Independent Social Democratic Party of Germany">Independent Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> (USPD); however, the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Landtag_elections_in_the_Weimar_Republic" title="Brunswick Landtag elections in the Weimar Republic">Landtag election</a> on 22 December 1918 was won by the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> (MSPD), and the USPD and MSPD formed a <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> An uprising in Braunschweig in 1919, led by the <a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">communist</a> <a href="/wiki/Spartacus_League" title="Spartacus League">Spartacus League</a>, was defeated when <i><a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">Freikorps</a></i> troops under <a href="/wiki/Georg_Ludwig_Rudolf_Maercker" title="Georg Ludwig Rudolf Maercker">Georg Ludwig Rudolf Maercker</a> took over the city on order of the German Minister of Defence, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Noske" title="Gustav Noske">Gustav Noske</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> An SPD-led government was subsequently established; in December 1921 a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a> was approved for the <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Brunswick" title="Free State of Brunswick">Free State of Brunswick</a>, now a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a>, again with Braunschweig as its capital.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Landtag election of 1930, Brunswick became the second state in Germany where the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazis</a> participated in government, when the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">National Socialist German Workers' Party</a> (NSDAP) formed a coalition government with several conservative and right-wing parties.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> With the support of <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Klagges" title="Dietrich Klagges">Dietrich Klagges</a>, Brunswick's minister of the interior, the NSDAP organized a large <a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">SA</a> rally in Braunschweig. On 17–18 October 1931, 100,000 SA stormtroopers marched through the city, street fights between Nazis, socialists and communists left several dead or injured.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On 25 February 1932, the state of Brunswick granted <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> German citizenship to allow him to run in the <a href="/wiki/German_presidential_election,_1932" title="German presidential election, 1932">1932 German presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In Braunschweig, Nazis carried out several attacks on political enemies, with the acquiescence of the state government.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_seizure_of_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi seizure of power">Nazi seizure of power</a> in 1933, several state institutions were placed in Braunschweig, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtforschungsanstalt" title="Luftfahrtforschungsanstalt">Luftfahrtforschungsanstalt</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkenrode" title="Völkenrode">Völkenrode</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hitler_Youth" title="Hitler Youth">Hitler Youth</a> <a href="/wiki/Academy_for_Youth_Leadership" title="Academy for Youth Leadership">Academy for Youth Leadership</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS" title="Waffen-SS">SS</a>-<a href="/wiki/Junker_Schools" title="Junker Schools">Junkerschule Braunschweig</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Reichswerke_Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Reichswerke Hermann Göring">Reichswerke Hermann Göring</a> in <a href="/wiki/Salzgitter" title="Salzgitter">Salzgitter</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wolfsburg" title="Wolfsburg">Stadt des KdF-Wagens</a>, as well as several factories in the city itself (including <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCssing" title="Büssing">Büssing</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagenwerk_Braunschweig" title="Volkswagenwerk Braunschweig">Volkswagenwerk Braunschweig</a>), the Braunschweig region became one of the centres of the German <a href="/wiki/Arms_industry" title="Arms industry">arms industry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, Braunschweig was an <i>Untergebiet Hauptquartier</i> ("Sub-Area Headquarters") of Wehrkreis XI ("<a href="/wiki/Military_district_(Germany)" title="Military district (Germany)">Military District XI</a>"),<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> and was the garrison city of the <a href="/wiki/31st_Infantry_Division_(Wehrmacht)" title="31st Infantry Division (Wehrmacht)">31st Infantry Division</a> that took part in the invasions of Poland, Belgium, and France, largely being destroyed during its retreat following the invasion of Russia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In this period, thousands of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern workers">Eastern workers</a> were brought to the city as <a href="/wiki/Forced_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced labor">forced labor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and in the 1943–1945 period at least 360 children taken away from such workers died in the <i><a href="/wiki/Ausl%C3%A4nderkinder-Pflegest%C3%A4tte" class="mw-redirect" title="Ausländerkinder-Pflegestätte">Entbindungsheim für Ostarbeiterinnen</a></i> ("Maternity Ward for Eastern Workers").<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Braunschweig_in_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombing of Braunschweig in World War II">Anglo-American air raid</a> on October 15, 1944 destroyed most of the city's churches, and the <i>Altstadt</i> (old town), the largest homogeneous ensemble of half-timbered houses in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The city's cathedral, which had been converted to a <i>Nationale Weihestätte</i> (<i>national shrine</i>) by the Nazi government, still stood.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar_period_to_the_21st_century">Postwar period to the 21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Postwar period to the 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Small sections of the city survived Allied bombing, and so remain to represent its distinctive architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The cathedral was restored to its function as a <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> church.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Politically, after the war, the Free State of Brunswick was dissolved by the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Occupation_Zones_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Allied Occupation Zones in Germany">Allied occupying authorities</a>, Braunschweig ceased to be a capital, and most of its lands were incorporated in the newly formed state of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, Braunschweig, then part of <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>, suffered economically due to its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a>. The city lost its historically strong economic ties to what was then <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>; for decades economic growth remained below and unemployment stayed above the West German average.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 February 1974, as part of a district reform in Lower Saxony, the <a href="/wiki/Landkreis" class="mw-redirect" title="Landkreis">rural district</a> of <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_(district)" title="Braunschweig (district)">Braunschweig</a>, which had surrounded the city, was disestablished. The major part of the former district was incorporated into the city of Braunschweig, increasing its population by roughly 52,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1990s, efforts increased to reconstruct historic buildings that had been destroyed in the air raid.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The façade of the <i><a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Palace" title="Brunswick Palace">Braunschweiger Schloss</a></i> was rebuilt, and buildings such as the <i>Alte Waage</i> (originally built in 1534) now stand again.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the population of Braunschweig was 252,768.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-47">[47]</a></sup> Today Braunschweig is among the twenty German cities found to be most attractive to young people between the ages of 25 and 34, leading to an influx of younger residents.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2015, 91,785 people or 36.3% of the population were <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Protestant</a> and 34,604 (13.7%) people were <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>. 126,379 people (50.0%) either adhered to other denominations or followed no religion.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A total of 64,737 of Braunschweig's residents, including German citizens, had an immigrant background in 2015 (25.6% of the total population).<sup id="cite_ref-Population_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-47">[47]</a></sup> Among those, 25,676 were non-German citizens (10.2%);<sup id="cite_ref-Population_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-47">[47]</a></sup> the following table lists up the largest minority groups:<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>The <i>Burgplatz</i> (Castle Square), comprising a group of buildings of great historical and cultural significance: the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Cathedral" title="Brunswick Cathedral">Cathedral</a> (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Blaise" title="Saint Blaise">St Blasius</a>, built at the end of the 12th century), the <i>Burg Dankwarderode</i> (Dankwarderode Castle) (a 19th-century reconstruction of the old castle of Henry the Lion), the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Gothic">Neo-Gothic</a> Town Hall (built in 1893–1900), as well as some picturesque <a href="/wiki/Timber_framing" title="Timber framing">half-timbered houses</a>, such as the <i>Gildehaus</i> (Guild House), today the seat of the Craftsman's Association. In the centre of the square stands a copy of the <i><a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Lion" title="Brunswick Lion">Burglöwe</a></i> (Brunswick Lion), a <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">Romanesque</a> statue of a Lion, cast in bronze in 1166. The original statue can be seen in the museum of Dankwarderode Castle. Today the lion has become the true symbol of Braunschweig.</li>
<li>The <i>Altstadtmarkt</i> ("Old Town market"), surrounded by the Old Town town hall (built between the 13th and the 15th centuries in Gothic style), and the <i>Martinikirche</i> (Church of <a href="/wiki/Martin_of_Tours" title="Martin of Tours">Saint Martin</a>, from 1195), with important historical houses including the <i><a href="/wiki/Cloth_hall" title="Cloth hall">Gewandhaus</a></i> (the former house of the drapers' guild, built sometime before 1268) and the <i>Stechinelli-Haus</i> (built in 1690) and a fountain from 1408.</li>
<li>The <i>Kohlmarkt</i> ("coal market"), a market with many historical houses and a fountain from 1869.</li>
<li>The <i>Hagenmarkt</i> ("<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Hag" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:Hag">Hagen</a> market"), with the 13th-century <i>Katharinenkirche</i> (Church of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Alexandria" title="Catherine of Alexandria">Saint Catherine</a>) and the <i>Heinrichsbrunnen</i> ("Henry the Lion's Fountain") from 1874.</li>
<li>The <i>Magniviertel</i> (<a href="/wiki/Magnus_of_Anagni" title="Magnus of Anagni">St Magnus</a>' Quarter), a remainder of ancient Braunschweig, lined with cobblestoned streets, little shops and cafés, centred around the 13th-century <i>Magnikirche</i> (St Magnus' Church). Here is also the <i>Rizzi-Haus</i>, a highly distinctive, cartoonish office building designed by architect <a href="/wiki/James_Rizzi" title="James Rizzi">James Rizzi</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Expo_2000" title="Expo 2000">Expo 2000</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> <i>Andreaskirche</i> (Church of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Andrew" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Andrew">Saint Andrew</a>), built mainly between the 13th and 16th centuries with stained glass by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Crodel" title="Charles Crodel">Charles Crodel</a>. Surrounding the church are the <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Brick_Gothic_buildings#Lower_Saxony_and_Bremen" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Brick Gothic buildings">Liberei</a></i>, the oldest surviving freestanding library building in Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and the reconstructed <i>Alte Waage</i>.</li>
<li>The Gothic <i><a href="/wiki/Aegidienkirche,_Braunschweig" title="Aegidienkirche, Braunschweig">Aegidienkirche</a></i> (Church of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Giles" title="Saint Giles">Saint Giles</a>), built in the 13th century, with an adjoining monastery, which is today a museum.</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_Braunschweig" title="Staatstheater Braunschweig">Staatstheater</a></i> (State Theatre), newly built in the 19th century, goes back to the first standing public theatre in Germany, founded in 1690 by Duke Anthony Ulrich.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Palace" title="Brunswick Palace">ducal palace of Braunschweig</a> was bombed in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and demolished in 1960. The exterior was rebuilt to contain a palace museum, library and shopping centre, which opened in 2007.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque</a> palace <i><a href="/wiki/Schloss_Richmond" title="Schloss Richmond">Schloss Richmond</a></i> ("Richmond Palace"), built between 1768 and 1769 with a surrounding <a href="/wiki/English_garden" class="mw-redirect" title="English garden">English garden</a> for <a href="/wiki/Princess_Augusta_of_Great_Britain" title="Princess Augusta of Great Britain">Princess Augusta of Great Britain</a>, wife of <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Ferdinand,_Duke_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Charles William Ferdinand, Duke of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Charles William Ferdinand, Duke of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel</a>, to remind her of her home in England.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Riddagshausen_Abbey" title="Riddagshausen Abbey">Riddagshausen Abbey</a> (German: <i>Kloster Riddagshausen</i>), a former <a href="/wiki/Cistercian" class="mw-redirect" title="Cistercian">Cistercian</a> monastery, with the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">arboretum</a>. The nature reserve <i>Riddagshäuser Teiche</i> is designated as <a href="/wiki/Important_Bird_Area" title="Important Bird Area">Important Bird Area</a><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Special_Protection_Area" title="Special Protection Area">Special Protection Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Parks and gardens in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_der_Technischen_Universit%C3%A4t_Braunschweig" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanischer Garten der Technischen Universität Braunschweig">Botanischer Garten der Technischen Universität Braunschweig</a></i>, founded in 1840 by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Heinrich_Blasius" title="Johann Heinrich Blasius">Johann Heinrich Blasius</a>, the <i>Bürgerpark</i>, the <i>Löwenwall</i> with an <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">obelisk</a> from 1825, the <i>Prinz-Albrecht-Park</i>, and the <i>Inselwallpark</i>. Other parks and <a href="/wiki/Recreation_area" title="Recreation area">recreation areas</a> are <i>Stadtpark</i>, <i>Westpark</i>, <i>Theaterpark</i>, <i>Museumpark</i>, <i>Heidbergsee</i>, <i>Südsee</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%96lper" title="Ölper">Ölpersee</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">zoological garden</a> <i>Arche Noah Zoo Braunschweig</i> and the nearby <a href="/wiki/Essehof_Zoo" title="Essehof Zoo">Essehof Zoo</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_(electoral_district)" title="Braunschweig (electoral district)">Braunschweig (electoral district)</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Braunschweig is made up of 19 <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">boroughs</a> (German: <i><a href="/wiki/Stadtbezirk" title="Stadtbezirk">Stadtbezirke</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> which themselves may consist of several quarters (German: <i>Stadtteile</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> each. The 19 boroughs, with their official numbers, are:</p>
<table class="toptextcells">
<tr>
<td style="width:25%;">
<ul>
<li>112: <a href="/wiki/Wabe-Schunter-Beberbach" title="Wabe-Schunter-Beberbach">Wabe-Schunter-Beberbach</a><sup>1</sup></li>
<li>113: <a href="/wiki/Hondelage" title="Hondelage">Hondelage</a></li>
<li>114: Volkmarode</li>
<li>120: <a href="/wiki/%C3%96stliches_Ringgebiet" title="Östliches Ringgebiet">Östliches Ringgebiet</a></li>
<li>131: <a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Braunschweig)" title="Innenstadt (Braunschweig)">Innenstadt</a></li>
<li>132: <a href="/wiki/Viewegsgarten-Bebelhof" title="Viewegsgarten-Bebelhof">Viewegsgarten-Bebelhof</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:25%;">
<ul>
<li>211: <a href="/wiki/St%C3%B6ckheim-Leiferde" title="Stöckheim-Leiferde">Stöckheim-Leiferde</a></li>
<li>212: <a href="/wiki/Heidberg-Melverode" title="Heidberg-Melverode">Heidberg-Melverode</a></li>
<li>213: Südstadt-Rautheim-Mascherode</li>
<li>221: <a href="/wiki/Weststadt_(Braunschweig)" title="Weststadt (Braunschweig)">Weststadt</a></li>
<li>222: Timmerlah-Geitelde-Stiddien</li>
<li>223: <a href="/wiki/Broitzem" title="Broitzem">Broitzem</a></li>
<li>224: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCningen" title="Rüningen">Rüningen</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:25%;">
<ul>
<li>310: Westliches Ringgebiet</li>
<li>321: <a href="/wiki/Lehndorf-Watenb%C3%BCttel" title="Lehndorf-Watenbüttel">Lehndorf-Watenbüttel</a></li>
<li>322: Veltenhof-Rühme</li>
<li>323: Wenden-Thune-Harxbüttel</li>
<li>331: Nordstadt</li>
<li>332: Schunteraue</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_council">City council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: City council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The council of the city is made up of the fractions of the different parties (54 seats) and the lord mayor, who is elected directly, with one seat.<sup id="cite_ref-Wahl_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wahl-56">[56]</a></sup> Since 2014, the lord mayor of Braunschweig is Ulrich Markurth (<a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">SPD</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Results of the most recent local elections on 11 September 2011<sup id="cite_ref-Wahl_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wahl-56">[56]</a></sup> and 11 September 2016<sup id="cite_ref-Wahl2_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wahl2-58">[58]</a></sup> were:</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr style="background:#e3e3e3">
<th>Party</th>
<th>2011<br />
% of vote (seats)</th>
<th>2016<br />
% of vote (seats)</th>
</tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th><a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany" title="Christian Democratic Union of Germany">Christian Democratic Union</a></th>
<td>38.2% (21)</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg/220px-Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg/330px-Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg/440px-Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ringerbrunnen_Braunschweig.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pedestrian zone in the city centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Braunschweig's city centre is mostly a car-free <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_zone" title="Pedestrian zone">pedestrian zone</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobile">Automobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Automobile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two main autobahns serve Braunschweig, the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_2" title="Bundesautobahn 2">A2</a> (<a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>—<a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a>—<a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_39" title="Bundesautobahn 39">A39</a> (<a href="/wiki/Salzgitter" title="Salzgitter">Salzgitter</a>—<a href="/wiki/Wolfsburg" title="Wolfsburg">Wolfsburg</a>). City roads are generally wide, built after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> to support the anticipated use of the automobile. There are several car parks in the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle">Bicycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Bicycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many residents travel around town by bicycle using an extensive system of bicycle-only lanes. The main train station includes a bicycle parking area.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city is on the main rail line between <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> and Berlin. <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> (German Railways) serves the city with local, inter-city and high-speed <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">InterCityExpress</a> (ICE) trains, with frequent stops at <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Braunschweig Central Station">Braunschweig Central Station</a> (German: <i>Braunschweig Hauptbahnhof</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram_and_bus">Tram and bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tram and bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg/220px-100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg/330px-100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg/440px-100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="1898" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:100_6771_0756_Rathaus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tram in Braunschweig</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Braunschweig" title="Trams in Braunschweig">Braunschweig tramway network</a> is an inexpensive and extensive 35&#160;km (22&#160;mi) long electric <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a> system. First opened in 1897, it has been modernized, including a 3.2&#160;km (2.0&#160;mi) extension in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The network has an <span class="nowrap">1,100&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft&#160;<span class="frac">7<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>5</sup>⁄<sub>16</sub></span>&#160;in</span>) <a href="/wiki/Track_gauge" title="Track gauge">gauge</a>, unique for a European railway or tramway network. However, it is being supplemented in stages by a third rail, to allow future joint working with the <span class="nowrap">1,435&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">4&#160;ft&#160;<span class="frac">8<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span>&#160;in</span>) <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">standard gauge</a></span> main railway network.</p>
<p>The municipally owned <a href="/wiki/Braunschweiger_Verkehrs-AG" title="Braunschweiger Verkehrs-AG">Braunschweiger Verkehrs-AG</a> currently operates five tram lines and several <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus</a> lines. The tram lines are:<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">

<th style="color:#fff; background:#039; text-align:center;">from</th>
<th style="color:#fff; background:#039; text-align:center;">to</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="padding:0 .4em; color:white; background:red; font-size:91%;"><b>Tram</b></span> <b>1</b></td>

</tr>

</tr>
