<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Braunschweig Airport">Braunschweig Airport</a> (BWE / EDVE) is located north of the city at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Braunschweig&amp;params=52_19_N_10_33_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">52°19′N</span> <span class="longitude">10°33′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">52.317°N 10.550°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">52.317; 10.550</span></span></span></a></span>, elev. 295&#160;ft (90&#160;m)</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Brunswick (disambiguation)">Brunswick (disambiguation)</a></div>
<p>Many other geographical locations around the world are named Brunswick, after the historical English name of Braunschweig. Between 1714 and 1837, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">House of Hanover</a> ruled Great Britain in <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Electorate of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Electorate of Brunswick-Lüneburg (Hanover)</a>. The House of Hanover was formally known as the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Welf" title="House of Welf">House of Brunswick-Lüneburg</a>, Hanover line.<sup id="cite_ref-heraldica_hanover_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heraldica_hanover-67">[67]</a></sup> As a result, many places in <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">the British colonies</a> were named after Brunswick, such as the province of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ironically, the city of Braunschweig was not ruled by the Hanoverians while its name was being given to other Brunswicks around the world. Starting in 1269, the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Duchy of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Duchy of Brunswick-Lüneburg</a> underwent a series of divisions and mergers, with parts of the territory being transferred between various branches of the family. The city of Braunschweig went to the senior branch of the house, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="List of rulers of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Wolfenbüttel line</a>, while <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCneburg" title="Lüneburg">Lüneburg</a> eventually ended up with the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">Hanover line</a>. Although the territory had been split, all branches of the family continued to style themselves as the House of Brunswick-Lüneburg.<sup id="cite_ref-heraldica_hanover_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heraldica_hanover-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-riedesel_1868_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riedesel_1868-69">[69]</a></sup> In 1884, the senior branch of the House of Welf became extinct. The Hanover line, being the last surviving line of the family, subsequently held the throne of the Duchy of Brunswick from November 1913 until November 1918.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_offices">Government offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Government offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The offices of the <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrt-Bundesamt" title="Luftfahrt-Bundesamt">Luftfahrt-Bundesamt</a> (LBA, "Federal Aviation Office") and the <a href="/wiki/German_Federal_Bureau_of_Aircraft_Accident_Investigation" title="German Federal Bureau of Aircraft Accident Investigation">German Federal Bureau of Aircraft Accident Investigation</a> (BFU) are located in Braunschweig.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_science">Research and science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Research and science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg/220px-Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg/330px-Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg/440px-Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="783" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig_altes_TU-Geb%C3%A4ude.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_University_of_Technology" title="Braunschweig University of Technology">Braunschweig University of Technology</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Braunschweig has been an important industrial area. Today it is known for its <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_University_of_Technology" title="Braunschweig University of Technology">University</a> and research institutes, mainly the <i>Johann Heinrich von Thuenen Institute</i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Julius_K%C3%BChn-Institut" title="Julius Kühn-Institut">Julius Kühn-Institut</a></i>, and the <i>Institute for Animal Food</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Loeffler_Institute" title="Friedrich Loeffler Institute">Friedrich Loeffler Institute</a>, until the end of 2007 all part of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Agricultural_Research_Centre" title="Federal Agricultural Research Centre">Federal Agricultural Research Centre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Sammlung_von_Mikroorganismen_und_Zellkulturen" title="Deutsche Sammlung von Mikroorganismen und Zellkulturen">German Collection of Microorganisms and Cell Cultures</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Physikalisch-Technische_Bundesanstalt" title="Physikalisch-Technische Bundesanstalt">Physikalisch-Technische Bundesanstalt</a> (PTB). The PTB Braunschweig maintains the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_clock" title="Atomic clock">atomic clock</a> responsible for the <a href="/wiki/DCF77" title="DCF77">DCF77</a> time signal and the official German time. In 2006 the region of Braunschweig was the most R&amp;D-intensive area in the whole <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> investing 7.1% of its GDP for research &amp; technology.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In 2014, the figure had risen to 7.7%, making Braunschweig retain its ranking as the most R&amp;D-intensive region in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat-5">[5]</a></sup> Braunschweig was named Germany's <i>City of Science 2007</i> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Stadt der Wissenschaft 2007</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Braunschweig University of Technology (German: <i>Technische Universität Braunschweig</i>) was founded in 1745 and is the oldest member of <a href="/wiki/TU9" title="TU9">TU9</a>, an incorporated society of the nine most prestigious, oldest, and largest universities focusing on engineering and technology in Germany. With approximately 18,000 students, Braunschweig University of Technology is the third largest university in Lower Saxony.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Also located in Braunschweig is the <i>Martino-Katharineum</i> (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martino-Katharineum_Braunschweig" class="extiw" title="de:Martino-Katharineum Braunschweig">German Wikipedia</a>), a secondary school founded in 1415. It had such famous pupils as <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss" title="Carl Friedrich Gauss">Carl Friedrich Gauss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoffmann_von_Fallersleben" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoffmann von Fallersleben">Hoffmann von Fallersleben</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dedekind" title="Richard Dedekind">Richard Dedekind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Spohr" title="Louis Spohr">Louis Spohr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Since 2004, Braunschweig also has an <i>International School</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Other notable secondary schools include <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_Gaussschule" title="Gymnasium Gaussschule">Gymnasium Gaussschule</a>, <i>Gymnasium Kleine Burg</i> (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gymnasium_Kleine_Burg" class="extiw" title="de:Gymnasium Kleine Burg">German Wikipedia</a>), <i>Hoffmann-von-Fallersleben-Schule Braunschweig</i> (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoffmann-von-Fallersleben-Schule_Braunschweig" class="extiw" title="de:Hoffmann-von-Fallersleben-Schule Braunschweig">German Wikipedia</a>), <i>Integrierte Gesamtschule Franzsches Feld</i> (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integrierte_Gesamtschule_Franzsches_Feld" class="extiw" title="de:Integrierte Gesamtschule Franzsches Feld">German Wikipedia</a>), and <i>Wilhelm-Gymnasium</i> (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm-Gymnasium_(Braunschweig)" class="extiw" title="de:Wilhelm-Gymnasium (Braunschweig)">German Wikipedia</a>).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a>'s only university of art, founded in 1963, can be found in Braunschweig, the <i><a href="/wiki/Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Bildende_K%C3%BCnste_Braunschweig" class="mw-redirect" title="Hochschule für Bildende Künste Braunschweig">Hochschule für Bildende Künste Braunschweig</a></i> (Braunschweig College of Fine Arts).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The HBK is an institution of higher artistic and scientific education and offers the opportunity to study for interdisciplinary artistic and scientific qualifications. Additionally, one of the campuses of the <a href="/wiki/Ostfalia_Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_angewandte_Wissenschaften" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostfalia Hochschule für angewandte Wissenschaften">Eastphalia University of Applied Sciences</a> (German: <i>Ostfalia Hochschule für angewandte Wissenschaften</i>, formerly <i>Fachhochschule Braunschweig/Wolfenbüttel</i>) was located in the city until 2010.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2015, the German weekly business news magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswoche" title="Wirtschaftswoche">Wirtschaftswoche</a></i> ranked Braunschweig as one of the most dynamic economic spaces in all of Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Braunschweig was one of the centres of the <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a> in Northern Germany. During the 19th and early 20th century the <a href="/wiki/Canning" title="Canning">canning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Railroad">railroad</a> industries and the <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> production were of great importance for Braunschweig's economy,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> but eventually other branches such as the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automotive industry</a> became more important, while especially the canning industry began to vanish from the city after the end of World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The defunct truck and bus manufacturer <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCssing" title="Büssing">Büssing</a> was headquartered in Braunschweig. Current <a href="/wiki/Factory" title="Factory">factories</a> in the city include <a href="/wiki/Volkswagenwerk_Braunschweig" title="Volkswagenwerk Braunschweig">Volkswagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier Transportation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a>.</p>
<p>The fashion label <a href="/wiki/NewYorker" title="NewYorker">NewYorker</a>, the publishing house <a href="/wiki/Westermann_Verlag" title="Westermann Verlag">Westermann Verlag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordzucker" title="Nordzucker">Nordzucker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Financial Services</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Bank</a> have their headquarters in the city as well as the Volkswagen utility vehicle holding. Also two major optical companies were headquartered in Braunschweig: <a href="/wiki/Voigtl%C3%A4nder" title="Voigtländer">Voigtländer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rollei" title="Rollei">Rollei</a>.</p>
<p>During the 1980s and early 1990s the <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computer</a> companies <a href="/wiki/Atari" title="Atari">Atari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commodore_International" title="Commodore International">Commodore International</a> both had branches for development and production within the city.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Braunschweig is the home of two <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> companies, both known worldwide for the high quality of their instruments: <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Schimmel" title="Wilhelm Schimmel">Schimmel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grotrian-Steinweg" title="Grotrian-Steinweg">Grotrian-Steinweg</a>. Both companies were founded in the 19th century. Additionally <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandberg_Guitars" class="extiw" title="de:Sandberg Guitars">Sandberg Guitars</a> is based in Braunschweig.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweigs_Industrie_(Postkarte_1904).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Braunschweigs_Industrie_%28Postkarte_1904%29.JPG/220px-Braunschweigs_Industrie_%28Postkarte_1904%29.JPG" width="220" height="334" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Braunschweigs_Industrie_%28Postkarte_1904%29.JPG/330px-Braunschweigs_Industrie_%28Postkarte_1904%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Braunschweigs_Industrie_%28Postkarte_1904%29.JPG/440px-Braunschweigs_Industrie_%28Postkarte_1904%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1213" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweigs_Industrie_(Postkarte_1904).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1904 <a href="/wiki/Postcard" title="Postcard">postcard</a> showing typical food of Braunschweig</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pieta.Kadishman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Pieta.Kadishman.jpg/220px-Pieta.Kadishman.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Pieta.Kadishman.jpg/330px-Pieta.Kadishman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/Pieta.Kadishman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pieta.Kadishman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Piëta</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Menashe_Kadishman" title="Menashe Kadishman">Menashe Kadishman</a>, Braunschweig</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Braunschweig is famous for <i><a href="/wiki/Till_Eulenspiegel" title="Till Eulenspiegel">Till Eulenspiegel</a></i>, a medieval jester who played many practical jokes on its citizens. It also had many breweries, and still a very peculiar kind of <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> is made called <i><a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Mum" title="Brunswick Mum">Mumme</a></i>, first quoted in 1390, a malt-extract that was shipped all over the world. Two major breweries still produce in Braunschweig, the <i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hofbrauhaus_Wolters" class="extiw" title="de:Hofbrauhaus Wolters">Hofbrauhaus Wolters</a></i>, founded in 1627, and the former <i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feldschl%C3%B6%C3%9Fchen_(Braunschweig)" class="extiw" title="de:Feldschlößchen (Braunschweig)">Feldschlößchen</a></i> brewery, founded in 1871, now operated by <a href="/wiki/Oettinger_Beer" class="mw-redirect" title="Oettinger Beer">Oettinger Beer</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Braunschweiger_(sausage)" title="Braunschweiger (sausage)">Braunschweiger</a> <a href="/wiki/Mettwurst" title="Mettwurst">Mettwurst</a>, a soft, spreadable smoked pork sausage, is named after the city. Other traditional local dishes include <a href="/wiki/Asparagus" title="Asparagus">white asparagus</a>, <i>Braunschweiger <a href="/wiki/Lebkuchen" title="Lebkuchen">Lebkuchen</a></i>, <i>Braunkohl</i> (a variant of <a href="/wiki/Kale" title="Kale">kale</a> served with <a href="/wiki/Bregenwurst" title="Bregenwurst">Bregenwurst</a>), and <i>Uhlen un Apen</i> (Low German for "<a href="/wiki/Owl" title="Owl">Owls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guenon" title="Guenon">Guenons</a>", a pastry).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Braunschweig's major local newspaper is the <i><a href="/wiki/Braunschweiger_Zeitung" title="Braunschweiger Zeitung">Braunschweiger Zeitung</a></i>, first published in 1946. Papers formerly published in Braunschweig include the <i>Braunschweigische Anzeigen</i>/<i>Braunschweigische Staatszeitung</i> (1745–1934), the <i>Braunschweigische Landeszeitung</i> (1880–1936) and the <i>Braunschweiger Stadtanzeiger</i>/<i>Braunschweiger Allgemeiner Anzeiger</i> (1886–1941), and the social-democratic <i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braunschweiger_Volksfreund" class="extiw" title="de:Braunschweiger Volksfreund">Braunschweiger Volksfreund</a></i> (1871–1933).</p>
<p>Near Braunschweig at <a href="/wiki/Cremlingen" title="Cremlingen">Cremlingen</a>-Abbenrode, there is a large medium wave transmitter, which transmits the program of <i><a href="/wiki/Deutschlandfunk" title="Deutschlandfunk">Deutschlandfunk</a></i> on 756&#160;kHz, the <a href="/wiki/Cremlingen_transmitter" title="Cremlingen transmitter">Cremlingen transmitter</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schoduvel" class="extiw" title="de:Schoduvel">Schoduvel</a></i>, a medieval Northern German form of <a href="/wiki/Carnival_in_Germany,_Switzerland_and_Austria" title="Carnival in Germany, Switzerland and Austria">carnival</a> was celebrated in Braunschweig as early as the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Since 1979 an annual <a href="/wiki/Rosenmontag" title="Rosenmontag">Rosenmontag</a> parade is held in Braunschweig, the largest in Northern Germany, which is named Schoduvel in honour of the medieval custom.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>An annual <i>Weihnachtsmarkt</i> (<a href="/wiki/Christmas_market" title="Christmas market">Christmas market</a>) is held in late November and December on the Burgplatz in the centre of Braunschweig. In 2008 the market had 900,000 visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_galleries">Museums and galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Museums and galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg/220px-Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg/330px-Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg/440px-Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="632" data-file-height="456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Braunschweig_Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum_nachts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Herzog Anton Ulrich Museum</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg/220px-Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg/330px-Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg/440px-Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="886" data-file-height="591" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salve_Hospes_04_1a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Villa Salve Hospes</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city's most important museum is the <a href="/wiki/Herzog_Anton_Ulrich_Museum" title="Herzog Anton Ulrich Museum">Herzog Anton Ulrich Museum</a>, a well known art museum and the oldest public museum in Germany, founded in 1754. It houses a collection of masters of Western art, including <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht Dürer">Dürer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giorgione" title="Giorgione">Giorgione</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Cranach_the_Elder" title="Lucas Cranach the Elder">Cranach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Holbein_the_Younger" title="Hans Holbein the Younger">Holbein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Dyck" title="Anthony van Dyck">Van Dyck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vermeer" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Vermeer">Vermeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Rubens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Braunschweigisches_Landesmuseum" title="Braunschweigisches Landesmuseum">State Museum of Brunswick</a> (<i>Braunschweigisches Landesmuseum</i>), founded in 1891, houses a permanent collection documenting the history of the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Land" title="Brunswick Land">Brunswick area</a> ranging from its early history to the present.</p>
<p>The Municipal Museum of Brunswick (<i>Städtisches Museum Braunschweig</i>), founded in 1861, is a museum for art and cultural history, documenting the history of the city of Braunschweig.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Naturhistorisches_Museum_(Braunschweig)" title="Naturhistorisches Museum (Braunschweig)">State Natural History Museum</a> is a zoology museum founded in 1754.</p>
<p>Other museums in the city include the Museum of Photography (<i>Museum für Photographie</i>), the Jewish Museum (<i>Jüdisches Museum</i>), the Museum for Agricultural Technology <i>Gut Steinhof</i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Gerst%C3%A4cker" title="Friedrich Gerstäcker">Gerstäcker-Museum</a>. Frequent exhibitions of contemporary art are also held by the Art Society of Braunschweig (German: <i>Kunstverein Braunschweig</i>), housed in the <i>Villa Salve Hospes</i>, a classicist villa built between 1805 and 1808.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Braunschweig_Classix_Festival" title="Braunschweig Classix Festival">Braunschweig Classix Festival</a></i> was an annual classical music festival. It is the largest promoter of classical music in the region and one of the most prominent music festivals in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a>.</p>
<p>From 2001 to 2009, and again since 2013, the annual finals of the international <a href="/wiki/Breakdance" class="mw-redirect" title="Breakdance">breakdance</a> competition <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Year" title="Battle of the Year">Battle of the Year</a> have been held at the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Halle" title="Volkswagen Halle">Volkswagen Halle</a> in Braunschweig.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Braunschweiger TSC</i> is among the leading competitive <a href="/wiki/Formation_dance" title="Formation dance">formation dance</a> teams in the world and has won multiple World and European championship titles.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg/220px-BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg/330px-BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg/440px-BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1736" data-file-height="1355" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BSM_Konrad-Koch_Braunschweig_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first German version of the rules of football by Konrad Koch</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG/220px-BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG/330px-BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG/440px-BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4352" data-file-height="3264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BS_Eintracht_Stadion.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eintracht-Stadion" title="Eintracht-Stadion">Eintracht-Stadion</a>, the stadium of <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Braunschweig" title="Eintracht Braunschweig">Eintracht Braunschweig</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Braunschweig's major local <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team is <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Braunschweig" title="Eintracht Braunschweig">Eintracht Braunschweig</a>. Founded in 1895, Eintracht Braunschweig can look back on a long and chequered history. Eintracht Braunschweig won the <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German football championship</a> in 1967, and currently plays in the <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a>, the second tier of German football, and attracts a large number of supporters. Braunschweig was also arguably the city in which the first ever game of football in Germany took place. The game had been brought to Germany by the local school teacher <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Koch" title="Konrad Koch">Konrad Koch</a>, also the first to write down a German version of the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_the_Game_(association_football)" title="Laws of the Game (association football)">rules of football</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[nb 1]</a></sup> who organized the first match between pupils from his school <i>Martino-Katharineum</i> in 1874.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> The 2011 German drama film <a href="/wiki/Lessons_of_a_Dream" title="Lessons of a Dream">Lessons of a Dream</a> is based on Koch.</p>
<p>Eintracht Braunschweig also fields a successful women's <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> team that claimed nine national championship titles between 1965 and 1978. In the past, the club also had first or second tier teams in the sports of <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_handball" title="Field handball">field handball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_Yorker_Lions" title="New Yorker Lions">New Yorker Lions</a> (formerly Braunschweig Lions) are the city's <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team, winning a record number of eleven <a href="/wiki/German_Bowl" title="German Bowl">German Bowl</a> titles, as well as five <a href="/wiki/Eurobowl" title="Eurobowl">Eurobowls</a> (a shared record).</p>
<p>The city's professional <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> team, the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_L%C3%B6wen_Braunschweig" title="Basketball Löwen Braunschweig">Basketball Löwen Braunschweig</a>, plays in the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Bundesliga" title="Basketball Bundesliga">Basketball Bundesliga</a>, the highest level in Germany. The Löwen's predecessor <a href="/wiki/SG_Braunschweig" title="SG Braunschweig">SG Braunschweig</a> had previously played in the Bundesliga as well. Eintracht Braunschweig's women's basketball team plays in the <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/2._Damen-Basketball-Bundesliga" class="extiw" title="de:2. Damen-Basketball-Bundesliga">2. Damen-Basketball-Bundesliga</a>, the second tier of women's basketball in Germany.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTV_Braunschweig" title="MTV Braunschweig">MTV Braunschweig</a>, the city's oldest sports club (founded in 1847), plays in the semi-professional <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/3._Liga_(Handball)" class="extiw" title="de:3. Liga (Handball)">3. Liga</a>.</p>
<p>Other sports clubs from Braunschweig that play or have played at the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Bundesliga (disambiguation)">Bundesliga</a> or <a href="/wiki/2nd_Bundesliga_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="2nd Bundesliga (disambiguation)">2nd Bundesliga</a> level include <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braunschweig_Spot_Up_89ers" class="extiw" title="de:Braunschweig Spot Up 89ers">Spot Up 89ers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>), <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braunschweiger_THC" class="extiw" title="de:Braunschweiger THC">Braunschweiger THC</a> (field hockey), <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Braunschweig" class="extiw" title="de:FC Braunschweig">SV Süd Braunschweig</a> (handball), <a href="/wiki/Rugby-Welfen_Braunschweig" title="Rugby-Welfen Braunschweig">Rugby-Welfen Braunschweig</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>), and <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/USC_Braunschweig" class="extiw" title="de:USC Braunschweig">USC Braunschweig</a> (<a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>).</p>
<p>Annual sporting events held in Braunschweig include the international <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> tournament <i>Löwen Classics</i>, <i>Rund um den Elm</i>, Germany's oldest <a href="/wiki/Road_bicycle_racing" title="Road bicycle racing">road bicycle race</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> and the professional <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> tournament <i><a href="/wiki/Sparkassen_Open" title="Sparkassen Open">Sparkassen Open</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Braunschweig" title="List of people from Braunschweig">List of people from Braunschweig</a></div>
<p>Alphabetical list of some notable people associated with Braunschweig:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hermann_Blumenau" title="Hermann Blumenau">Hermann Blumenau</a> (1819–1899), founder of <a href="/wiki/Blumenau" title="Blumenau">Blumenau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Joachim_Christoph_Bode" title="Johann Joachim Christoph Bode">Johann Joachim Christoph Bode</a> (1731–1793), translator<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bosse_(musician)" title="Bosse (musician)">Bosse</a> (born 1980), rock musician<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Bracke" class="extiw" title="de:Wilhelm Bracke">Wilhelm Bracke</a> (1842–1880), one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Workers%27_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Workers' Party of Germany">Social Democratic Workers' Party of Germany</a>, predecessor of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCssing" title="Büssing">Heinrich Büssing</a> (1843–1929), industrialist<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Axel_Freiherr_von_dem_Bussche-Streithorst" class="mw-redirect" title="Axel Freiherr von dem Bussche-Streithorst">Axel Freiherr von dem Bussche-Streithorst</a> (1919–1993), military officer and member of the <a href="/wiki/German_resistance" class="mw-redirect" title="German resistance">German resistance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joachim_Heinrich_Campe" title="Joachim Heinrich Campe">Joachim Heinrich Campe</a> (1746–1818), educator and writer<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caroline_of_Brunswick" title="Caroline of Brunswick">Caroline of Brunswick</a> (1768–1821), <a href="/wiki/Queen_consort" title="Queen consort">Queen consort</a> of King <a href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">George IV of the United Kingdom</a><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Dedekind" title="Richard Dedekind">Richard Dedekind</a> (1831–1916), mathematician<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Drude" title="Paul Drude">Paul Drude</a> (1863–1906), physicist, developed the <a href="/wiki/Drude_model" title="Drude model">Drude model</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christine_Enghaus" title="Christine Enghaus">Christine Enghaus</a> (1815–1910), actress<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Joachim_Eschenburg" title="Johann Joachim Eschenburg">Johann Joachim Eschenburg</a> (1743–1820), produced the first complete German translation of <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>'s plays.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_William,_Duke_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Frederick William, Duke of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Frederick William, Duke of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel</a> (1771–1815), leader of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Brunswickers" title="Black Brunswickers">Black Brunswickers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarck1_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarck1-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss" title="Carl Friedrich Gauss">Carl Friedrich Gauss</a> (1777–1855), mathematician<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Gerst%C3%A4cker" title="Friedrich Gerstäcker">Friedrich Gerstäcker</a> (1816–1872), writer<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Glogowski" title="Gerhard Glogowski">Gerhard Glogowski</a> (born 1943), politician<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otto_Grotewohl" title="Otto Grotewohl">Otto Grotewohl</a> (1894–1964), <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">Prime minister</a> of the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">German Democratic Republic</a><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otto_Harder" title="Otto Harder">Otto Harder</a> (1892–1956), German international footballer<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adolph_Henke" title="Adolph Henke">Adolph Henke</a> (1775–1843), physician<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Lion" title="Henry the Lion">Henry the Lion</a> (1129–1195), <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Saxony" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Saxony">Duke of Saxony</a> <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Bavaria">and Bavaria</a><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/August_Hermann" title="August Hermann">August Hermann</a> (1835–1906), "Braunschweig's Father of Physical Education"<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/August_Heinrich_Hoffmann_von_Fallersleben" title="August Heinrich Hoffmann von Fallersleben">August Heinrich Hoffmann von Fallersleben</a> (1798–1874), poet and author of <i><a href="/wiki/Deutschlandlied" title="Deutschlandlied">Das Lied der Deutschen</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ricarda_Huch" title="Ricarda Huch">Ricarda Huch</a> (1864–1947), historian and writer<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ernst_August_Friedrich_Klingemann" title="Ernst August Friedrich Klingemann">Ernst August Friedrich Klingemann</a> (1777–1831), writer<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gustav_Knuth" title="Gustav Knuth">Gustav Knuth</a> (1901–1987), actor<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kubel" title="Alfred Kubel">Alfred Kubel</a> (1909–1999), politician<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/August_Lafontaine" title="August Lafontaine">August Lafontaine</a> (1758–1831), author of sentimental didactic novels once immensely popular, born and brought up in the city<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Anton_Leisewitz" title="Johann Anton Leisewitz">Johann Anton Leisewitz</a> (1752–1806), poet<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gotthold_Ephraim_Lessing" title="Gotthold Ephraim Lessing">Gotthold Ephraim Lessing</a> (1729–1781), writer and philosopher<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otto_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto IV of Brunswick</a> (1175–1218), <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Plockhorst" title="Bernhard Plockhorst">Bernhard Plockhorst</a> (1825–1907), painter<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agnes_Pockels" title="Agnes Pockels">Agnes Pockels</a> (1862–1935), chemist<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Raabe" title="Wilhelm Raabe">Wilhelm Raabe</a> (1831–1910), writer<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Adolf_Riedesel" title="Friedrich Adolf Riedesel">Friedrich Adolf Riedesel</a> (1738–1800), commander during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Galka_Scheyer" title="Galka Scheyer">Galka Scheyer</a> (1889–1945), painter<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dennis_Schr%C3%B6der" title="Dennis Schröder">Dennis Schröder</a> (born 1993), NBA basketball player, currently with the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks" title="Atlanta Hawks">Atlanta Hawks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norbert_Schultze" title="Norbert Schultze">Norbert Schultze</a> (1911–2002), composer<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hans_Sommer_(composer)" title="Hans Sommer (composer)">Hans Sommer</a> (1837–1922), composer and mathematician<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louis_Spohr" title="Louis Spohr">Louis Spohr</a> (1784–1859), composer<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_E._Steinway" title="Henry E. Steinway">Henry E.</a> (1797–1871) and <a href="/wiki/C.F._Theodore_Steinway" title="C.F. Theodore Steinway">C.F. Theodore Steinway</a> (1825–1889), piano makers<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ludger_Tom_Ring_the_Younger" title="Ludger Tom Ring the Younger">Ludger Tom Ring the Younger</a> (1522–1584), painter<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Georg_Weitsch" title="Friedrich Georg Weitsch">Friedrich Georg Weitsch</a> (1758–1828), painter<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Braunschweig&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">However, Koch's original German version of the rules of football, published in 1875, still resembled <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">Rugby football</a> - the unmodified rules of <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a> weren't commonly used in Germany before the 1900s.</span></li>
</ol>

<li><sup><small>1</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a> were both capital of the Westphalian Quarter at different times.</li>
<li><sup><small>2</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> gained importance once <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> became inaccessible due to the silting of the <a href="/wiki/Zwin" title="Zwin">Zwin</a> channel.</li>
